## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x and time t. In classical mechanics, the acceleration is determined by the restoring force, which for nonlinear oscillators includes higher-order terms in displacement beyond the linear Hooke's law term, and may include damping and driving forces dependent on time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator restoring force)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (nonlinear spring force)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic driving)
- Nonlinear damped driven: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum restoring torque)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Van der Pol-like: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * x (nonlinear damping term approximation)
- Rational nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (bounded restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear oscillator)
- Position-time coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * t (time-varying stiffness)
- Exponential restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x * exp(c1 * x**2) (exponentially stiffening spring)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells typical of Duffing-type oscillators
- Sinusoidal dependence on position sin(c*x) → pendulum-like systems with periodic potential energy
- Time-periodic terms sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external driving forces or parametric excitation
- Mixed even and odd powers of x → asymmetric potential indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Product terms x*cos(c*t) or x*sin(c*t) → parametric resonance or time-modulated spring constant
- Acceleration purely a function of x (no explicit t) → autonomous conservative or dissipative system
- Sign of cubic coefficient relative to linear term → hardening (same sign as linear) vs softening (opposite sign) spring
- Rational functions of x → bounded force models preventing divergence at large displacements

**Candidate 10:** `c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*t*x + c3*x³ + c4*x⁵`
Set c4=0: x, sin(t), t*x, x³. ✓

= c0 + c1*sin(t) + c2*x³ + c3*x + c4*t*x + c5*x*sin(c6*t+c7)

**Candidate 13:** `c0*sin(t) + x*(c1*x² + c2 + c3*t + c4*sin(c5*t+c6))`
Set c4=0: sin(t), x³, x, t*x. ✓
Candidate 13 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** `c0*sin(c1*(c2*x + c3*t)) + x*(c4*x² + c5 + c6*t)`
sin(c1*c2*x + c1*c3*t) — this is sin of a linear combination of x and t. This cannot equal sin(t) for all x unless c1*c2=0. If c1*c2=0 and c1*c3≠0, then sin(c1*c3*t). Set c1*c3=1: sin(t). Then x*(c4*x²+c5+c6*t) = c4*x³+c5*x+c6*t*x. ✓
Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 15:** `c0*x + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*sin(t) + c5*t*x + c6*x³`
Set c1=0: x, sin(t), t*x, x³. ✓ (Or combine sin terms if c2=1.)
Candidate 15 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 16:** `c0*sin(t) + c1*x³*cos(c2*t) + x*(c3*x² + c4 + c5*t)`
= c0*sin(t) + c1*x³*cos(c2*t) + c3*x³ + c4*x + c5*t*x

cos(c1*x) with c1=0 → 1. Then: c0*sin(t) + c2*x³ + c3*x + c4*t*x. ✓
Candidate 17 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 18:** `c0*x + c1*sin(c2+t) + c3*x³ + c4*t*x`
sin(c2+t) = sin(c2)cos(t) + cos(c2)sin(t). This introduces cos(t) unless sin(c2)=0, i.e., c2=0 or c2=nπ. Set c2=0: sin(t). Result: x, sin(t), x³, t*x. ✓
